>   (b) any person who is the landlord or licensor in relation to a person occupying the house under a tenancy or licence.

- (7) After subsection (3) insert—

> (3A) In proceedings against a person for an offence under subsection [(1)](#p13968)[(a)](#p13971) it is a defence for them to prove that they had a reasonable excuse—
>   (a) for having control of or managing the house, or
>   (b) for being the landlord or licensor in relation to a person occupying the house under a tenancy or licence,
> in circumstances in which the house was required to be licensed under this Part but was not so licensed.
> (3B) In proceedings against a person for an offence under subsection [(1)](#p13968)[(b)](#p13976) it is a defence for them to prove that they—
>   (a) did not know, and had a reasonable excuse for not knowing, that the house was one to which this Part applies,
>   (b) took all reasonably practicable steps to ensure that the house was licensed under this Part, or
>   (c) had some other reasonable excuse for failing to ensure that the house was so licensed.
> (3C) For the purposes of subsection [(3B)](#p14018), a term in the tenancy agreement or licence to occupy relating to the occupation of the house does not on its own constitute a defence under any of paragraphs [(a)](#p14023) to [(c)](#p14031) of that subsection.

- (8) In subsection (4)—

- (a) for “subsection (1) or (2)” substitute “subsection (2)”, and

- (b) for the words following “excuse” substitute “for failing to comply with the condition”.

#### Service of improvement notices on landlords and licensors

##### 106

In Schedule 1 to the [Housing Act 2004](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2004/34) (procedure and appeals relating to improvement notices), in paragraph 2(2)—

- (a) after “the notice” insert “on whichever of the following the authority considers ought to take the action specified in it”,

- (b) in paragraphs (a) and (b), omit “on” in each place, and

- (c) after [paragraph (b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/106/b/2025-12-27) insert—

> (c) (in either case) if the premises or any part of them are let under a tenancy that is periodic or was granted for a term of 21 years or less, or are occupied under a licence—
>   (i) the landlord or licensor;
>   (ii) any superior landlord or licensor.

### Chapter 2 — Enforcement authorities

#### Enforcement by local housing authorities: general duty

##### 107

- (1) It is the duty of every local housing authority to enforce the landlord legislation in its area.

- (2) But the duty in [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/107/1/2025-12-27) does not prevent a local housing authority from taking enforcement action in respect of a breach of, or an offence under, the landlord legislation which occurs outside of its area.

- (3) The duty is also subject to [sections 108](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/108/2025-12-27)[(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/108/3/2025-12-27) (enforcement by another local housing authority), [109](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/109/2025-12-27)[(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/109/3/2025-12-27) (enforcement by county council in England which is not a local housing authority) and [113](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/2025-12-27)[(4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/4/2025-12-27) (enforcement by the lead enforcement authority).

- (4) A county council in England which is not a local housing authority may—

- (a) enforce the landlord legislation;

- (b) for that purpose, exercise any powers that a local housing authority may exercise for the purposes of enforcing that legislation.

- (5) In [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/2025-12-27) “*the landlord legislation*” means—

- (a) [Chapters 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/chapter/3/2025-12-27) and [6](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/chapter/6/2025-12-27) of [Part 1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/2025-12-27) of this Act,

- (b) [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27) of this Act,

- (c) sections 1 and 1A of the [Protection from Eviction Act 1977](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1977/43), and

- (d) Chapter 1 of Part 1 of [the 1988 Act](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1988/50).

- (6) For the purposes of [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/2025-12-27), a reference to taking enforcement action is a reference to—

- (a) imposing a financial penalty, or

- (b) instituting proceedings against a person for an offence,

under the landlord legislation.

#### Enforcement by local housing authorities: duty to notify

##### 108

- (1) Where a local housing authority (“LA1”) proposes to take enforcement action in respect of a breach of, or an offence under, the landlord legislation which occurs (or which also occurs) in the area of another local housing authority (“LA2”), LA1 must notify LA2 that it proposes to do so.

- (2) If LA1 notifies LA2 under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/108/1/2025-12-27) but does not take the action referred to in [that subsection](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/108/1/2025-12-27), LA1 must notify LA2 of that fact.

- (3) Where a local housing authority receives a notification under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/108/1/2025-12-27), the authority is relieved of the duty under [section 107](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/107/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/107/1/2025-12-27) in relation to the breach or offence unless the authority receives a notification under [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/108/2/2025-12-27).

- (4) [Subsection (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/108/5/2025-12-27) applies where—

- (a) a local housing authority (“LA1”) has imposed a financial penalty under the landlord legislation,

- (b) the breach or offence to which the penalty relates occurred in the area of another local housing authority (“LA2”), and

- (c) the final notice imposing the penalty has not been withdrawn.

- (5) LA1 must notify LA2 as soon as reasonably practicable if—

- (a) the period for bringing an appeal against the penalty expires without an appeal being brought,

- (b) an appeal against the penalty is withdrawn or abandoned, or

- (c) the final notice imposing the penalty is confirmed or varied on appeal.

- (6) [Subsection (7)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/108/7/2025-12-27) applies where—

- (a) a local housing authority (“LA1”) has instituted proceedings against a person for an offence under the landlord legislation, and

- (b) the conduct to which the offence relates occurred in the area of another local housing authority (“LA2”).

- (7) LA1 must notify LA2 as soon as reasonably practicable if the person is convicted of the offence.

#### Enforcement by county councils: duty to notify

##### 109

- (1) A county council in England—

- (a) which is not a local housing authority, and

- (b) which proposes to take enforcement action in respect of a breach of, or an offence under, the landlord legislation,

must notify any local housing authority in whose area the breach or offence occurred.

- (2) If the county council notifies a local housing authority under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/109/1/2025-12-27) but does not take the action referred to in [that subsection](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/109/1/2025-12-27), it must notify the local housing authority of that fact.

- (3) Where a local housing authority receives a notification under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/109/1/2025-12-27), the authority is relieved of the duty under [section 107](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/107/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/107/1/2025-12-27) in relation to the breach or offence unless the authority receives notification under [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/109/2/2025-12-27).

- (4) [Subsection (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/109/5/2025-12-27) applies where—

- (a) a county council in England which is not a local housing authority has imposed a financial penalty in respect of a breach of, or an offence under, the landlord legislation, and

- (b) the final notice imposing the penalty has not been withdrawn.

- (5) The county council must as soon as reasonably practicable notify any local housing authority in whose area the breach or offence occurred if—

- (a) the period for bringing an appeal against the penalty expires without an appeal being brought,

- (b) an appeal against the penalty is withdrawn or abandoned, or

- (c) the final notice imposing the penalty is confirmed or varied on appeal.

- (6) A county council in England—

- (a) which is not a local housing authority, and

- (b) which institutes proceedings against a person for an offence under the landlord legislation,

must as soon as reasonably practicable notify any local housing authority in whose area the offence occurred if the person is convicted of the offence.

#### Duty to report

##### 110

- (1) A local housing authority, or a county council which is not a local housing authority, must report to the Secretary of State on the exercise of its functions under the landlord legislation.

- (2) A report under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/110/1/2025-12-27) must—

- (a) be provided at such time and in such form as the Secretary of State requires, and

- (b) contain such information as the Secretary of State requires.

#### Lead enforcement authority

##### 111

- (1) The Secretary of State may make arrangements for a relevant person to be the lead enforcement authority for the purposes of any provisions of the landlord legislation.

- (2) The arrangements may include arrangements—

- (a) for payments by the Secretary of State;

- (b) about bringing the arrangements to an end.

- (3) The Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory instrument make transitional or saving provision which applies when there is a change in the lead enforcement authority for any provisions of the landlord legislation.

- (4) The regulations may relate to a specific change in the lead enforcement authority or to changes that might arise from time to time.

- (5) In [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/2025-12-27)—

- “*lead enforcement authority*” means a relevant person which the Secretary of State has arranged to be a lead enforcement authority under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/111/1/2025-12-27);

- “*relevant person*” means— a combined authority established under section 103 of the [Local Democracy, Economic Development and Construction Act 2009](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2009/20), the Greater London Authority, or a local housing authority.

- (6) For the purposes of [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/2025-12-27), a lead enforcement authority is “responsible” for the provisions of the landlord legislation for the purposes of which it is such an authority under arrangements made under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/111/1/2025-12-27).

#### General duties and powers of lead enforcement authority

##### 112

- (1) A lead enforcement authority must oversee the operation of the provisions for which it is responsible.

- (2) A lead enforcement authority must provide—

- (a) relevant local authorities, and

- (b) the public in England,

with information and advice about the operation of the provisions for which it is responsible, in such form and manner as the lead enforcement authority considers appropriate.

- (3) A lead enforcement authority may disclose information to a relevant local authority for the purposes of enabling that authority to determine whether there has been a breach of, or an offence under, the provisions for which the lead enforcement authority is responsible.

- (4) A lead enforcement authority may issue guidance to relevant local authorities about the exercise of their functions under any of the provisions for which it is responsible.

- (5) Relevant local authorities must have regard to any guidance issued under [subsection (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/112/4/2025-12-27).

- (6) A lead enforcement authority must keep under review and from time to time advise the Secretary of State about the following—

- (a) the operation of the landlord provisions for which it is responsible;

- (b) social and commercial developments relating to tenancies in England, other than tenancies of social housing, so far as it considers those developments relevant to the provisions for which it is responsible.

- (7) The Secretary of State may give a lead enforcement authority directions as to the exercise of any of its functions.

- (8) A direction may relate to all or particular kinds of relevant local authorities and may make different provision for different purposes.

- (9) In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/112/2025-12-27)—

- “*relevant local authority*” means— a local housing authority, or a county council in England which is not a local housing authority;

- “*social housing*” has the same meaning as in Part 2 of the [Housing and Regeneration Act 2008](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2008/17);

- “*tenancies*” includes licences to occupy.

#### Enforcement by the lead enforcement authority

##### 113

- (1) A lead enforcement authority may—

- (a) take steps to enforce the provisions for which it is responsible where it considers it necessary or expedient to do so;

- (b) for that purpose, exercise any powers that a local housing authority may exercise for the purpose of the enforcement of those provisions.

- (2) Where a lead enforcement authority proposes to take steps under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/1/2025-12-27) in respect of a breach of, or an offence under, the provisions for which it is responsible, it must notify the local housing authority in whose area the breach or offence occurred that it proposes to do so.

- (3) If a lead enforcement authority notifies a local housing authority under [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/2/2025-12-27) but does not take the steps referred to in [that subsection](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/2/2025-12-27), the lead enforcement authority must notify the local housing authority of that fact.

- (4) Where a local housing authority receives a notification under [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/2/2025-12-27), the authority is relieved of the duty under [section 107](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/107/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/107/1/2025-12-27) in relation to the breach or offence unless the authority receives a notification under [subsection (3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/3/2025-12-27).

- (5) But a lead enforcement authority may require a local housing authority to assist the lead enforcement authority in taking the steps referred to in [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/1/2025-12-27).

- (6) A relevant local authority must report to a lead enforcement authority, whenever the lead enforcement authority requires and in such form and with such particulars as it requires, on the exercise of that relevant local authority’s functions under the provisions for which the lead enforcement authority is responsible.

- (7) The powers of a local housing authority referred to in [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/1/2025-12-27)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/1/b/2025-12-27) include the power to authorise persons to exercise powers of officers under [Chapter 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) (see section [132](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/132/2025-12-27)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/132/2/2025-12-27)).

- (8) [Section 126](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27)[(10)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/10/2025-12-27) is to be read, in relation to an officer of a lead enforcement authority, as if—

- (a) the reference to a deputy chief officer whose duties relate to a purpose within [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/b/2025-12-27) of [that section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27) were a reference to—

- (i) a person who is employed by, or acts on the instructions of, the body which is the lead enforcement authority and has overall responsibility for the exercise of the functions of that body in that capacity (“*the head of the lead enforcement authority*”), or

- (ii) a person who is employed by, or acts on the instructions of, the lead enforcement authority, and has been authorised by the head of the lead enforcement authority to give special authorisations within the meaning of [section 126](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27), and

- (b) [paragraph (b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/10/b/2025-12-27)[(ii)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/10/b/ii/2025-12-27) were omitted.

- (9) In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/113/2025-12-27) “*relevant local authority*” has the same meaning as in [section 112](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/112/2025-12-27).

### Chapter 3 — Investigatory powers

### Investigatory powers under this Act

#### Power of local housing authority to require information from relevant person

##### 114

- (1) An officer of a local housing authority may, for purposes connected with any function of the authority under or by virtue of legislation set out in the list in [subsection (3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/114/3/2025-12-27), give a notice to a relevant person requiring the person to provide the local housing authority or an officer with the information specified in the notice.

- (2) In [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) “*relevant person*”, in relation to a power under [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27), means a person who has, in the twelve months ending with the day on which the power is exercised—

- (a) had an estate or interest in premises which consist of or include any relevant accommodation, otherwise than as a mortgagee not in possession,

- (b) been a licensor of premises which consist of or include any relevant accommodation,

- (c) acted or purported to act on behalf of a person within [paragraph (a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/114/2/a/2025-12-27) or [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/114/2/b/2025-12-27), or

- (d) marketed any relevant accommodation for the purposes of creating a residential tenancy, within the meaning of [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27) (see section [99](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/99/2025-12-27)).

- (3) Here is the list—

- sections 1 and 1A of the [Protection from Eviction Act 1977](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1977/43);

- Chapter 1 of Part 1 of the [Housing Act 1988](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1988/50);

- section 83(1) or 84(1) of the [Enterprise and Regulatory Reform Act 2013](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2013/24)*;*

- sections 21 to 23 of the [Housing and Planning Act 2016](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2016/22);

- [Chapter 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/chapter/3/2025-12-27) of [Part 1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/2025-12-27) and [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27) of this Act.

- (4) A notice under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/114/2025-12-27) must be in writing and must specify that it is given under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/114/2025-12-27).

- (5) The notice may specify—

- (a) the time within which and the manner in which the relevant person to whom it is given must comply with it;

- (b) the form in which information must be provided.

- (6) The notice may require—

- (a) the creation of documents, or documents of a description, specified in the notice, and

- (b) the provision of those documents to an enforcement authority or officer.

- (7) The notice must include information about the possible consequences of not complying with a notice under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/114/2025-12-27).

- (8) A requirement to provide information or create a document is a requirement to do so in a legible form.

- (9) A notice under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/114/2025-12-27) does not require a person to provide any information or create any documents which the person would be entitled to refuse to provide or produce in proceedings in the High Court on the grounds of legal professional privilege.

- (10) In [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/114/2/2025-12-27) “*relevant accommodation*” means any residential accommodation in England that is connected with the exercise or proposed exercise of the function in relation to which the power under [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) is exercised.

#### Power of local housing authority to require information from any person

##### 115

- (1) Where an officer of a local housing authority reasonably suspects that there has been a breach of, or an offence under, the rented accommodation legislation, the officer may for a purpose mentioned in [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/2/2025-12-27) give notice to any person requiring the person to provide the local housing authority or an officer with information specified in the notice.

- (2) The purposes are—

- (a) investigating whether there has been a breach of, or an offence under, the rented accommodation legislation, or

- (b) determining the amount of a penalty under that legislation.

- (3) In [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) “*the rented accommodation legislation*” means—

- sections 1 and 1A of the [Protection from Eviction Act 1977](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1977/43);

- Chapter 1 of Part 1 of the [Housing Act 1988](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1988/50);

- Parts 1 to 4 and 7 of the [Housing Act 2004](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2004/34) so far as relating to qualifying residential premises within the meaning given by section 2B of [that Act](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2004/34);

- section 83(1) or 84(1) of the [Enterprise and Regulatory Reform Act 2013](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2013/24)*;*

- sections 21 to 23 of the [Housing and Planning Act 2016](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2016/22);

- [Chapter 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/chapter/3/2025-12-27) of [Part 1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/2025-12-27) and [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27) of this Act.

- (4) A notice under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/2025-12-27) must be in writing and must specify that it is given under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/2025-12-27).

- (5) The notice may specify—

- (a) the time within which and the manner in which the person to whom it is given must comply with it;

- (b) the form in which information must be provided.

- (6) The notice may require—

- (a) the creation of documents, or documents of a description, specified in the notice, and

- (b) the provision of those documents to an enforcement authority or officer.

- (7) The notice must include information about the possible consequences of not complying with a notice under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/2025-12-27).

- (8) A requirement to provide information or create a document is a requirement to do so in a legible form.

#### Enforcement of power to require information from any person

##### 116

- (1) If a person fails to comply with a notice under [section 115](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/2025-12-27), the local housing authority or an officer of the authority may make an application under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/116/2025-12-27) to the court.

- (2) If it appears to the court that the person has failed to comply with the notice, it may make an order under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/116/2025-12-27).

- (3) An order under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/116/2025-12-27) is an order requiring the person to do anything that the court thinks it is reasonable for the person to do, for any of the purposes for which the notice was given, to ensure that the notice is complied with.

- (4) An order under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/116/2025-12-27) may require the person to meet the costs of the application.

- (5) If the person is a company, partnership or unincorporated association, the court in acting under [subsection (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/116/4/2025-12-27) may require an official who is responsible for the failure to meet the costs or expenses.

- (6) In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/116/2025-12-27)—

- “*the court*” means— the High Court, or the county court;

- “*official*” means— in the case of a company, a director, manager, secretary or other similar officer, in the case of a limited liability partnership, a member, in the case of a partnership other than a limited liability partnership, a partner, and in the case of an unincorporated association, a person who is concerned in the management or control of its affairs.

#### Limitation on use of information provided under section 115

##### 117

- (1) In any criminal proceedings against a person who provides information in response to a notice under [section 115](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/2025-12-27) (including information contained in a document created in response to such a notice)—

- (a) no evidence relating to the information may be adduced by or on behalf of the prosecution, and

- (b) no question relating to the information may be asked by or on behalf of the prosecution.

- (2) [Subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/117/1/2025-12-27) does not apply if, in the proceedings—

- (a) evidence relating to the information is adduced by or on behalf of the person providing it, or

- (b) a question relating to the information is asked by or on behalf of that person.

- (3) [Subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/117/1/2025-12-27) does not apply if the proceedings are for an offence under section 5 of the Perjury Act 1911 (false statutory declarations and other false statements without oath).

#### Business premises: entry without warrant

##### 118

- (1) An officer of a local housing authority may, at any reasonable time, enter any premises in England if—

- (a) the officer reasonably believes the premises to be occupied by a relevant person for the purposes of a rental sector business, and

- (b) the officer considers it necessary to enter the premises in order to exercise the powers under [section 122](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/2025-12-27) or [123](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/2025-12-27) for purposes connected with any function of the authority under or by virtue of the rented accommodation legislation.

- (2) [Subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/1/2025-12-27) does not authorise entry into premises used wholly or mainly as residential accommodation.

- (3) In the case of a routine inspection, the power in [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/1/2025-12-27) may only be exercised if a notice has been given to an occupier of the premises in accordance with the requirements in [subsection (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/4/2025-12-27), unless [subsection (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/5/2025-12-27) applies.

- (4) Those requirements are that—

- (a) the notice is in writing and is given by an officer of the local housing authority,

- (b) the notice sets out why the entry is necessary and indicates the nature of the offences under [section 131](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/1/2025-12-27) and [(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/2/2025-12-27), and

- (c) there are at least 24 hours between the giving of the notice and the entry.

- (5) A notice need not be given if the occupier (or one of the occupiers if there is more than one) has waived the requirement to give notice.

- (6) In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/2025-12-27) “*routine inspection*” means an exercise of the power in [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/1/2025-12-27) other than where—

- (a) the officer reasonably considers that to give notice in accordance with [subsection (3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/3/2025-12-27) would defeat the purpose of the entry, or

- (b) it is not reasonably practicable in all the circumstances to give notice in accordance with [that subsection](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/3/2025-12-27).

- (7) An officer entering premises under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/1/2025-12-27) may be accompanied by such persons, and may take onto the premises such equipment, as the officer thinks necessary.

- (8) An officer entering premises under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/1/2025-12-27) may take photographs or make recordings.

- (9) In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/2025-12-27) “*rental sector business*” means a business connected with—

- (a) the letting of residential accommodation in England,

- (b) the creation of licences to occupy such accommodation,

- (c) the marketing of such accommodation for the purpose of creating a tenancy or licence to occupy, or

- (d) the management of such accommodation when occupied under a tenancy or licence to occupy.

#### Duties where occupiers are on business premises entered without warrant

##### 119

- (1) If an officer of a local housing authority enters premises under [section 118](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/1/2025-12-27) and finds one or more occupiers on the premises, the officer must—

- (a) produce evidence of the officer’s identity and authority to that occupier or (if there is more than one) to at least one of them, and

- (b) if the entry takes place otherwise than in the course of a routine inspection, provide to that occupier or (if there is more than one) to at least one of them a document that—

- (i) sets out why the entry is necessary, and

- (ii) indicates the nature of the offences under [section 131](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/1/2025-12-27) and [(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/2/2025-12-27).

- (2) An officer need not comply with [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/119/1/2025-12-27) if it is not reasonably practicable to do so.

- (3) Proceedings resulting from the exercise of the power under [section 118](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/1/2025-12-27) are not invalid merely because of a failure to comply with [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/119/1/2025-12-27).

#### Business premises: warrant authorising entry

##### 120

- (1) A justice of the peace may issue a warrant authorising an officer of a local housing authority who is named in the warrant to enter premises in England that are specified in the warrant if the justice of the peace is satisfied, on written information on oath given by that officer—

- (a) that the officer would, in entering the premises, be acting in the course of employment by, or on the instructions of, the local housing authority, and

- (b) that there are reasonable grounds for believing that—

- (i) the premises are occupied by a relevant person for the purposes of a rental sector business,

- (ii) the premises are not used wholly or mainly as residential accommodation,

- (iii) on the premises there are documents which an officer of the local housing authority could require a person to produce under [section 122](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/2025-12-27), or could seize under [section 123](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/2025-12-27), and

- (iv) condition A, B or C is met.

- (2) Condition A is that—

- (a) access to the premises has been or is likely to be refused, and

- (b) notice of the local housing authority’s intention to apply for a warrant under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/120/2025-12-27) has been given to an occupier of the premises.

- (3) Condition B is that it is likely that documents on the premises would be concealed or interfered with if notice of entry of the premises were given to an occupier of the premises.

- (4) Condition C is that no occupier is present, and it might defeat the purpose of the entry to wait for their return.

- (5) In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/120/2025-12-27) “*rental sector business*” has the meaning given by [section 118](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/2025-12-27)[(9)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/9/2025-12-27).

#### Business premises: entry under warrant

##### 121

- (1) A warrant under [section 120](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/120/2025-12-27) authorises the officer named in the warrant to enter the premises at any reasonable time, using reasonable force if necessary.

- (2) A warrant under [that section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/120/2025-12-27) does not authorise entry into premises used wholly or mainly as residential accommodation.

- (3) A warrant under [that section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/120/2025-12-27) ceases to have effect at the end of the period of one month beginning with the day it is issued.

- (4) An officer entering premises under a warrant under [section 120](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/120/2025-12-27) may be accompanied by such persons, and may take onto the premises such equipment, as the officer thinks necessary.

- (5) An officer entering premises under a warrant under [section 120](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/120/2025-12-27) may take photographs or make recordings.

- (6) If, when the officer enters the premises, the officer finds one or more occupiers on the premises, the officer must produce the warrant for inspection to that occupier or (if there is more than one) to at least one of them.

- (7) [Subsection (8)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/121/8/2025-12-27) applies if no occupier is present when the premises are entered.

- (8) On leaving the premises the officer must—

- (a) leave a notice on the premises stating that the premises have been entered under a warrant under [section 120](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/120/2025-12-27), and

- (b) leave the premises as effectively secured against trespassers as the officer found them.

#### Power to require production of documents following entry

##### 122

- (1) An officer of a local housing authority who has entered premises under [section 118](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/1/2025-12-27) or under a warrant under [section 120](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/120/2025-12-27) may, for the purposes mentioned in [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/2/2025-12-27), at any reasonable time—

- (a) require a relevant person occupying the premises, or anyone on the premises acting on behalf of such a person, to produce any documents relating to the relevant business to which the person on the premises has access, and

- (b) take copies of, or of any entry in, any such document.

- (2) The purposes are—

- (a) to ascertain whether there has been compliance with the rented accommodation legislation where an officer of the local housing authority reasonably suspects a breach of, or an offence under, that legislation;

- (b) to ascertain whether the documents may be required as evidence in proceedings for such a breach or offence.

- (3) The power in [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/1/2025-12-27) is available regardless of whether—

- (a) the purpose for which the documents are required relates to the relevant person or some other person, or

- (b) the proceedings referred to in [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/2/2025-12-27)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/2/b/2025-12-27) could be taken against the relevant person or some other person.

- (4) That power includes power to require the person to give an explanation of the documents.

- (5) Where a document required to be produced under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/1/2025-12-27) contains information recorded electronically, the power in [that subsection](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/1/2025-12-27) includes power to require the production of a copy of the document in a form in which it can easily be taken away and in which it is visible and legible.

- (6) [This section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/2025-12-27) does not permit an officer to require a person to create a document other than as described in [subsection (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/5/2025-12-27).

- (7) [This section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/2025-12-27) does not permit an officer to require a person to produce any document which the person would be entitled to refuse to produce in proceedings in the High Court on the grounds of legal professional privilege.

- (8) In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/2025-12-27) “*relevant business*” means the business for the purposes of which the premises are occupied.

#### Power to seize documents following entry

##### 123

- (1) An officer of a local housing authority who has entered premises under [section 118](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/1/2025-12-27) or under a warrant under [section 120](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/120/2025-12-27) may seize and detain documents which the officer reasonably suspects may be required as evidence in proceedings relating to a breach of, or an offence under, the rented accommodation legislation.

- (2) If one or more occupiers are on the premises, an officer seizing documents under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/2025-12-27) must provide to that occupier or (if there is more than one) to at least one of them evidence of the officer’s identity and authority, before seizing the documents.

- (3) The officer need not comply with [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/2/2025-12-27) if it is not reasonably practicable to do so.

- (4) An officer seizing documents under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/2025-12-27) must take reasonable steps to—

- (a) inform the person from whom they are seized that they have been seized, and

- (b) provide that person with a written record of what has been seized.

- (5) In determining the steps to be taken under [subsection (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/4/2025-12-27), an officer exercising a power under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/2025-12-27) must have regard to any relevant provision about the seizure of property made by a code of practice under section 66 of the [Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1984/60).

- (6) [This section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/2025-12-27) does not confer any power on an officer to seize from a person any document which the person would be entitled to refuse to produce in proceedings in the High Court on the grounds of legal professional privilege.

- (7) For the purpose of exercising the power under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/2025-12-27), the officer may, to the extent that is reasonably necessary for that purpose—

- (a) require a person with authority to do so to access any electronic device in which information may be stored or from which it may be accessed, and

- (b) if such a requirement has not been complied with, access the electronic device.

- (8) Documents seized under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/2025-12-27) may not be detained—

- (a) for a period of more than 3 months beginning with the day on which they were seized, or

- (b) where the documents are reasonably required to be detained for a longer period by the local housing authority for the purposes of the proceedings for which they were seized, for longer than they are required for those purposes.

#### Access to seized documents

##### 124

- (1) [This section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/124/2025-12-27) applies where any document seized by an officer of a local housing authority under [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) is detained by the officer or authority.

- (2) If a request for permission to be granted access to that document is made to the local housing authority by a person who had custody or control of it immediately before it was seized, the local housing authority must allow that person access to it under the supervision of an officer.

- (3) If a request for a photograph or copy of that document is made to the local housing authority by a person who had custody or control of it immediately before it was seized, the local housing authority must—

- (a) allow that person access to it under the supervision of an officer for the purpose of photographing or copying it, or

- (b) photograph or copy it, or cause it to be photographed or copied.

- (4) Where any document is photographed or copied under [subsection (3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/124/3/2025-12-27), the photograph or copy must be supplied to the person who made the request within a reasonable time from the making of the request.

- (5) [This section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/124/2025-12-27) does not require access to be granted to, or a photograph or copy to be supplied of, any document if the local housing authority has reasonable grounds for believing that to do so would prejudice the doing of anything for the purposes of which it was seized.

- (6) A local housing authority may recover the reasonable costs of complying with a request under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/124/2025-12-27) from the person by whom or on whose behalf it was made.

- (7) References in [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/124/2025-12-27) to a person who had custody or control of a document immediately before it was seized include a representative of such a person.

#### Appeal against detention of documents

##### 125

- (1) Where documents are being detained as the result of the exercise of a power in [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27), a person with an interest in the documents may apply for an order requiring them to be released to that or another person.

- (2) An application under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/125/2025-12-27) may be made—

- (a) to any magistrates’ court in which proceedings have been brought for an offence as the result of the investigation in the course of which the documents were seized, or

- (b) if no proceedings within [paragraph (a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/125/2/a/2025-12-27) have been brought, by way of complaint to a magistrates’ court.

- (3) On an application under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/125/2025-12-27), the court may make an order requiring documents to be released only if satisfied that condition A or B is met.

- (4) Condition A is that—

- (a) no proceedings have been brought for an offence as the result of the investigation in the course of which the documents were seized, or

- (b) the period of 6 months beginning with the date the documents were seized has expired.

- (5) Condition B is that—

- (a) proceedings of a kind mentioned in [subsection (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/125/4/2025-12-27)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/125/4/a/2025-12-27) have been brought, and

- (b) those proceedings have been concluded.

- (6) A person aggrieved by an order made under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/125/2025-12-27) by a magistrates’ court, or by the decision of a magistrates’ court not to make such an order, may appeal against the order or decision to the Crown Court.

- (7) An order made under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/125/2025-12-27) by a magistrates’ court may contain such provision as the court thinks appropriate for delaying its coming into force pending the making and determination of any appeal.

#### Suspected residential tenancy: entry without warrant

##### 126

- (1) A specially authorised officer of a local housing authority may enter premises in England at any reasonable time, if—

- (a) the officer reasonably suspects that the premises, or part of the premises, are subject to a residential tenancy within the meaning of [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27) (see section [63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/63/2025-12-27)), and

- (b) the officer considers it necessary to inspect the premises for the purpose of investigating whether there has been, in relation to the premises—

- (i) a breach of [section 82](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/82/2025-12-27)[(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/82/3/2025-12-27),

- (ii) an offence under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/1/2025-12-27) of [section 92](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2025-12-27),

- (iii) an offence under [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2/2025-12-27) of [section 92](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2025-12-27) where the continuing conduct referred to in [paragraph (b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2/b/2025-12-27) of [that subsection](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2/2025-12-27) is a breach of [section 82](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/82/2025-12-27)[(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/82/3/2025-12-27),

- (iv) an offence under [subsection (3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/3/2025-12-27) of [section 92](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2025-12-27) where the different breach referred to in [paragraph (b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/3/b/2025-12-27) of [that subsection](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/3/2025-12-27) is a breach of [section 82](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/82/2025-12-27)[(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/82/3/2025-12-27),

- (v) an offence under [subsection (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/4/2025-12-27) of [section 92](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2025-12-27) where the breach referred to in [paragraph (b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/4/b/2025-12-27) of [that subsection](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/4/2025-12-27) is a breach of [section 82](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/82/2025-12-27)[(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/82/3/2025-12-27), or

- (vi) an offence under section 1 of the [Protection from Eviction Act 1977](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1977/43), and

- (c) notice has been given in accordance with the requirements of [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2/2025-12-27) to—

- (i) an occupier of the premises, and

- (ii) any person who has an estate or interest in the premises, other than a mortgagee not in possession and has supplied the local housing authority with an address for the purposes of [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/c/2025-12-27),

unless notice is not required as a result of [subsection (3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/3/2025-12-27) or [(4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/4/2025-12-27).

- (2) The requirements referred to in [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27)[(c)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/c/2025-12-27) are that—

- (a) the notice is in writing and is given by an officer of the local housing authority,

- (b) the notice sets out why the entry is necessary and indicates the nature of the offences under [section 131](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/1/2025-12-27) and [(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/2/2025-12-27) (obstruction), and

- (c) there are at least 24 hours between the giving of the notice and the entry.

- (3) A notice need not be given to a person who has waived the requirement to give notice.

- (4) A notice need not be given in accordance with subsection [(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27)[(c)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/c/2025-12-27)[(ii)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/c/ii/2025-12-27) to a person who is a residential landlord within the meaning of Part [2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27) (see section [63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/63/2025-12-27)).

- (5) If—

- (a) premises are entered in exercise of the power conferred by subsection [(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27), and

- (b) notice is not given to any person because of subsection [(4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/4/2025-12-27),

an officer of the local housing authority must give that person notice in writing of the exercise of that power within a reasonable period after its exercise.

- (6) The notice must—

- (a) identify the premises that were entered,

- (b) state when the premises were entered, and

- (c) state the purpose for which the premises were entered.

- (7) A specially authorised officer entering premises under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27) may be accompanied by such persons, and may take onto the premises such equipment, as the officer thinks necessary.

- (8) A specially authorised officer entering premises under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27) may take photographs or make recordings.

- (9) A specially authorised officer must, if requested to do so, produce the officer’s special authorisation for inspection by a person to whom notice is required to be given under [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27) or anyone acting on behalf of such a person.

- (10) For the purposes of [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27) an officer of a local housing authority is “specially authorised” where the officer’s authorisation by the local housing authority for the purposes of the power under [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27) (see section [132](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/132/2025-12-27)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/132/2/2025-12-27))—

- (a) states the particular purpose for which the officer is authorised to exercise the power, and

- (b) is given by the local housing authority acting through—

- (i) a deputy chief officer of the authority whose duties include duties relating to a purpose within [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/b/2025-12-27), or

- (ii) an officer of the authority to whom such a deputy chief officer reports directly, or is directly accountable, as respects duties so relating.

#### Duties where occupiers are on residential premises entered without warrant

##### 127

- (1) If an officer of a local housing authority enters premises under [section 126](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27) and finds one or more occupiers on the premises, the officer must produce evidence of the officer’s identity and special authorisation to that occupier or (if there is more than one) to at least one of them.

- (2) An officer need not comply with [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/127/1/2025-12-27) if it is not reasonably practicable to do so.

- (3) Proceedings resulting from the exercise of the power under [section 126](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27) are not invalid merely because of a failure to comply with [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/127/1/2025-12-27).

- (4) In [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/127/2025-12-27) “*special authorisation*” has the same meaning as in [section 126](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27) (see subsection (10) of that section).

#### Suspected residential tenancy: warrant authorising entry

##### 128

A justice of the peace may issue a warrant authorising an officer of a local housing authority who is named in the warrant to enter premises in England that are specified in the warrant if the justice of the peace is satisfied, on written information on oath given by that officer—

- (a) that the officer would, in entering the premises, be acting in the course of employment by, or on the instructions of, the local housing authority,

- (b) that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that the premises, or part of the premises, are subject to a residential tenancy within the meaning of [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27) (see section [63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/63/2025-12-27)),

- (c) that it is necessary for the officer to inspect the premises for the purpose of investigating whether there has been, in relation to the premises, a breach or an offence mentioned in [section 126](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/b/2025-12-27),

- (d) that—

- (i) admission to the premises has been sought for the purposes of entry under [section 126](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27) but has been refused,

- (ii) that no occupier is present and it might defeat the purpose of the entry to await their return, or

- (iii) that application for admission would defeat the purpose of the entry.

#### Suspected residential tenancy: entry under warrant

##### 129

- (1) A warrant under [section 128](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/128/2025-12-27) authorises the officer named in the warrant to enter the premises at any reasonable time, using reasonable force if necessary.

- (2) A warrant under [that section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/128/2025-12-27) ceases to have effect when the inspection of the premises has been completed.

- (3) An officer entering premises under a warrant under [section 128](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/128/2025-12-27) may be accompanied by such persons, and may take onto the premises such equipment, as the officer thinks necessary.

- (4) An officer entering premises under [section 128](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/128/2025-12-27) may take photographs or make recordings.

- (5) If, when the officer enters the premises, the officer finds one or more occupiers on the premises, the officer must produce the warrant for inspection to that occupier or (if there is more than one) to at least one of them.

- (6) [Subsection (7)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/129/7/2025-12-27) applies if no occupier is present when the premises are entered.

- (7) On leaving the premises the officer must—

- (a) leave a notice on the premises stating that the premises have been entered under a warrant under [section 128](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/128/2025-12-27), and

- (b) leave the premises as effectively secured against trespassers as the officer found them.

#### Powers of accompanying persons

##### 130

A person who accompanies an officer of a local housing authority entering premises under, or under a warrant under, [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27)—

- (a) has the same powers under [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) as the officer in relation to the premises, but

- (b) must exercise those powers only in the company, and under the supervision, of the officer.

#### Offences

##### 131

- (1) A person commits an offence if the person—

- (a) without reasonable excuse obstructs an officer of a local housing authority who is exercising or seeking to exercise in accordance with [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) a power under any provision of [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) other than [section 115](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/2025-12-27),

- (b) without reasonable excuse fails to comply with a requirement properly imposed by an officer of a local housing authority under any provision of [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) other than [section 115](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/2025-12-27), or

- (c) without reasonable cause fails to give an officer of a local housing authority any other assistance or information which the officer reasonably requires of the person for the purpose of exercising a power under any provision of [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) other than [section 115](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/2025-12-27).

- (2) A person commits an offence if, in giving information to an officer who is exercising or seeking to exercise a power under this Chapter, the person—

- (a) makes a statement which the person knows is false or misleading in a material respect, or

- (b) recklessly makes a statement which is false or misleading in a material respect.

- (3) A person who is not an officer of a local housing authority commits an offence if the person purports to act as such under this Chapter.

- (4) A person who is guilty of an offence under subsection [(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/1/2025-12-27) or [(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/2/2025-12-27) is liable on summary conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.

- (5) A person who is guilty of an offence under subsection [(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/3/2025-12-27) is liable on summary conviction to a fine.

- (6) Nothing in this section requires a person to answer any question or give any information if to do so might incriminate that person.

#### Investigatory powers: interpretation

##### 132

- (1) In this Chapter—

- “*document*” includes information recorded in any form;

- “*give*”— in relation to a notice to an occupier of premises, includes delivering or leaving it at the premises or sending it there by post, and “*given*”, in relation to such a notice, is to be read accordingly; in relation to a notice to a person referred to in [section 126](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/2025-12-27)[(c)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/c/2025-12-27)[(ii)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/126/1/c/ii/2025-12-27), includes delivering or leaving it at the address supplied by the person or sending it to that address by post, and “*given*”, in relation to such a notice, is to be read accordingly;

- “*occupier*”, in relation to premises, means any person an officer of a local housing authority reasonably suspects to be an occupier of the premises;

- “*premises*” includes any stall, vehicle, vessel or aircraft;

- “*relevant person*”: see [section 114](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/114/2025-12-27)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/114/2/2025-12-27);

- “*the rented accommodation legislation*”: see [section 115](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/2025-12-27)[(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/115/3/2025-12-27).

- (2) References in [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) to an officer—

- (a) are to a person authorised in writing by a local housing authority to exercise powers under [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27), and

- (b) in relation to a particular power only cover a particular officer if and to the extent that the officer has been authorised to exercise that power.

- (3) References in [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) to the functions of a local housing authority by virtue of particular legislation include references to any function of the authority of investigating whether an offence has been committed under that legislation.

- (4) A duty or power to process information that is imposed or conferred by, or by virtue of, [this Chapter](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/4/chapter/3/2025-12-27) does not operate to authorise the processing of information which would contravene—

- (a) the data protection legislation (but the duty or power is to be taken into account in determining whether the processing would contravene that legislation), or

- (b) [Parts 1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2016/25/contents#pt_1) to 7 or Chapter 9 of the [Investigatory Powers Act 2016](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2016/25).

- (5) In [subsection (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2018/12/#sec_3__subsec_4) “*the data protection legislation*” has the same meaning as in the [Data Protection Act 2018](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2018/12) (see section 3 of that Act).

### Amendments

#### Additional powers of seizure under Criminal Justice and Police Act 2001

##### 133

In Part 1 of Schedule 1 to the [Criminal Justice and Police Act 2001](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2001/16), at the end insert—

> (73W) Each of the powers of seizure conferred by section [122](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/1/2025-12-27)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/122/1/b/2025-12-27) and section [123](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/123/2025-12-27) of the Renters’ Rights Act 2025.

#### Use by local housing authority of certain information

##### 134

- (1) Section 212A of the [Housing Act 2004](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2004/34) (tenancy deposit schemes: provision of information to local authorities) is amended in accordance with [subsections (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/134/2/2025-12-27) and [(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/134/3/2025-12-27).

- (2) In subsection (5), after paragraph (a) (but before the “or” at the end) insert—

> (aa) for a purpose connected with the exercise of the authority’s functions under or by virtue of Part 7 in relation to any qualifying residential premises within the meaning given by section 2B,
> (ab) for a purpose connected with the authority’s functions under or by virtue of the following in relation to any premises—
>   - sections 1 and 1A of the [Protection from Eviction Act 1977](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1977/43),
>   - Chapter 1 of Part 1 of the [Housing Act 1988](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1988/50),
>   - section 83(1) or 84(1) of the [Enterprise and Regulatory Reform Act 2013](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2013/24)*,*
>   - sections 21 to 23, 41 and 133 to 135 of the [Housing and Planning Act 2016](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2016/22),
>   - [Chapter 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/chapter/3/2025-12-27) of [Part 1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/2025-12-27) and [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27) of the Renters’ Rights Act 2025.

.

- (3) In [subsection (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/134/5/2025-12-27), in paragraph (b), for “of those Parts in relation to any premises” substitute “provision mentioned in paragraphs (a) to [(ab)](#p16057) in relation to premises or qualifying residential premises (as the case may be)”.

- (4) Section 237 of the [Housing Act 2004](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2004/34) (use of housing benefit and council tax information for certain other statutory purposes) is amended in accordance with [subsections (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/134/5/2025-12-27) and [(6)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/134/6/2025-12-27).

- (5) In subsection (1), after paragraph (a) (but before the “or” at the end) insert—

> (aa) for any purpose connected with the exercise of any of the authority’s functions under or by virtue of Part 7 in relation to any qualifying residential premises within the meaning given by section 2B,
> (ab) for any purpose connected with any of the authority’s functions under or by virtue of the following in relation to any premises—
>   - sections 1 and 1A of the [Protection from Eviction Act 1977](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1977/43),
>   - Chapter 1 of Part 1 of the [Housing Act 1988](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1988/50),
>   - section 83(1) or 84(1) of the [Enterprise and Regulatory Reform Act 2013](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2013/24)*,*
>   - sections 21 to 23, 41 and 133 to 135 of the [Housing and Planning Act 2016](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2016/22),
>   - [Chapter 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/chapter/3/2025-12-27) of [Part 1](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/1/2025-12-27) and [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27) of the Renters’ Rights Act 2025.

.

- (6) In subsection (1), in paragraph (b), for “of those Parts in relation to any premises” substitute “provision mentioned in paragraphs (a) to (ab) in relation to premises or qualifying residential premises (as the case may be).

#### Investigatory powers under the Housing Act 2004

##### 135

- (1) In section 235 of the [Housing Act 2004](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2004/34) (power to require documents to be produced), in subsection (1)—

- (a) after [paragraph (a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/135/1/a/2025-12-27) (but before the “or” at the end) insert—

> (aa) for any purpose connected with the exercise of any of the authority’s functions under this Part in relation to any qualifying residential premises within the meaning given by section 2B,

;

- (b) in paragraph (b) for “those Parts in relation to any premises” substitute “Parts 1 to 4 in relation to any premises or under this Part in relation to any qualifying residential premises within the meaning given by section 2B”.

- (2) In section 239 of [that Act](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2004/34) (powers of entry), after subsection (5) insert—

> (5A) In relation to any qualifying residential premises within the meaning given by section 2B, notice need not be given—
>   (a) to any owner;
>   (b) to any occupier who has waived the requirement to give notice.
> (5B) If—
>   (a) premises are entered in exercise of the power conferred by subsection (3), and
>   (b) notice is not given to any person because of subsection [(5A)](#p16145)[(a)](#p16148),
> the authorised person or proper officer must give that person notice of the exercise of that power within a reasonable period after its exercise.
> (5C) The notice must—
>   (a) identify the premises that were entered,
>   (b) state when the premises were entered, and
>   (c) state the purpose for which the premises were entered.

#### Client money protection schemes: investigatory powers of local authorities

> - regulations 5 and 8 of the [Client Money Protection Schemes for Property Agents (Requirement to Belong to a Scheme etc.) Regulations 2019](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/uksi/2019/386)

.

## Part 5 — General

#### Interpretation

##### 137

In this Act—

- “*lease*” includes any tenancy;

- “*local housing authority*” (except in [section 47](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/47/2025-12-27)) means a district council, a county council in England for an area for which there is no district council, a London borough council, the Common Council of the City of London (in its capacity as a local authority) or the Council of the Isles of Scilly;

- “*the 1988 Act*” means the [Housing Act 1988](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1988/50).

#### Crown application

##### 138

- (1) Subject to [subsections (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/138/2/2025-12-27) to [(8)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/138/8/2025-12-27), this Act and any regulations made under it bind the Crown.

- (2) [Sections 67](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2025-12-27) and [92](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2025-12-27) do not bind the Crown.

- (3) In [paragraph (b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/66/1/b/2025-12-27) of [section 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/66/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/66/1/2025-12-27) as it applies by virtue of [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/138/1/2025-12-27), the reference to a person committing an offence under [section 67](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2025-12-27) is to be read as a reference to the person satisfying the conditions in [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/1/2025-12-27)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/1/a/2025-12-27) and [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/1/b/2025-12-27), [(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2/2025-12-27)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2/a/2025-12-27) and [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2/b/2025-12-27), or (3)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/3/a/2025-12-27) and [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/3/b/2025-12-27) of [that section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2025-12-27).

- (4) In [paragraph (b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/91/1/b/2025-12-27) of [section 91](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/91/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/91/1/2025-12-27) as it applies by virtue of [subsection (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/138/1/2025-12-27), the reference to a person committing an offence under [section 92](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2025-12-27) is to be read as a reference to the person either—

- (a) knowingly or recklessly providing information to the database operator which is false or misleading in a material respect in purported compliance with a requirement imposed by regulations under [Chapter 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/chapter/3/2025-12-27) of [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27), or

- (b) satisfying the conditions in [subsection (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2/2025-12-27)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2/a/2025-12-27) and [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2/b/2025-12-27), [(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/3/2025-12-27)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/3/a/2025-12-27) and [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/3/b/2025-12-27), or [(4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/4/2025-12-27)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/4/a/2025-12-27) and [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/4/b/2025-12-27) of [section 92](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2025-12-27).

- (5) [Sections 118](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/118/2025-12-27) to [130](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/130/2025-12-27) do not bind the Crown.

- (6) Nothing in [section 131](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/2025-12-27) makes the Crown criminally liable.

- (7) The High Court may declare unlawful any act or omission for which the Crown would be criminally liable under [section 131](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/131/2025-12-27) but for [subsection (6)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/138/6/2025-12-27).

- (8) An amendment or repeal made by this Act binds the Crown to the extent that the provision amended or repealed binds the Crown (but in the case of an amendment of [the 1988 Act](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/1988/50), this is subject to the amendments made by [section 18](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/18/2025-12-27)).

- (9) Nothing in [this section](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/138/2025-12-27) affects the criminal liability of persons in the service of the Crown.

#### Application to Parliament

##### 139

- (1) Where regulations under [section 63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/63/2025-12-27)[(4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/63/4/2025-12-27)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/63/4/b/2025-12-27) provide for the meaning of “relevant tenancy” given by that section to include a tenancy or licence under which a dwelling is occupied for the purposes of either House of Parliament, [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27) (and [Part 3](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/3/2025-12-27) so far as relating to [Part 2](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/part/2/2025-12-27)) has effect in its application in relation to such a tenancy or licence with the following modifications—

- (a) [sections 67](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2025-12-27) and [92](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/92/2025-12-27) do not apply;

- (b) in paragraph [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/66/1/b/2025-12-27) of [section 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/66/2025-12-27)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/66/1/2025-12-27), the reference to a person committing an offence under [section 67](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2025-12-27) is to be read as a reference to the person satisfying the conditions in subsection [(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/1/2025-12-27)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/1/a/2025-12-27) and [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/1/b/2025-12-27), [(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2/2025-12-27)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2/a/2025-12-27) and [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/2/b/2025-12-27), or [(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/3/2025-12-27)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/3/a/2025-12-27) and [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2025/26/section/67/3/b/2025-12-27) of that section;
